  YoungAdults >= 10
- Number of young adults should be at least a third the number of senior citizens:
  YoungAdults >= 1/3 * Seniors

Objective:
- Minimize the total wage bill:
  Minimize 500 * Seniors + 750 * YoungAdults
```python

from cpmpy import Model, intvar

# Decision Variables
Seniors = intvar(0, 999999999)  # Number of senior citizens employed
YoungAdults = intvar(0, 999999999)  # Number of young adults employed

# Constraints

# Weekly wage bill should be below $30000:

# At least 50 workers are required:

# At least 10 workers must be young adults:

# Number of young adults should be at least a third the number of senior citizens:
m += YoungAdults >= 1/3 * Seniors

  500 * PremiumDesktops + 300 * RegularDesktops
```python

from cpmpy import Model, intvar

# Decision Variables
PremiumDesktops = intvar(0, 999999999)  # Number of premium desktops made and sold
RegularDesktops = intvar(0, 999999999)  # Number of regular desktops made and sold

# Constraints
m = Model()

# The store sells at most 200 desktops each month:
m += PremiumDesktops + RegularDesktops <= 200
# The store wants to spend at most $300000 on making the desktops:
m += 2000 * PremiumDesktops + 1000 * RegularDesktops <= 300000

# Objective
# Maximize profit ($500 profit per premium desktop, $300 profit per regular desktop):
m.maximize(500 * PremiumDesktops + 300 * RegularDesktops)

- Number of mangos sold: Mangos
- Number of guavas sold: Guavas

- The food truck owner can spend at most $20000 on mangos and guavas:

- Number of servings of vegetables: Vegetables
- Number of servings of fruits: Fruits

Constraints:
- Each serving of vegetables contains 2 units of vitamins and 3 units of minerals:
  2 * Vegetables <= Vitamins
  3 * Vegetables <= Minerals
- Each serving of fruits contains 4 units of vitamins and 1 unit of minerals:

- He wants to eat at least 20 units of vitamins and 30 units of minerals:
  Vitamins >= 20
  Minerals >= 30

Objective:
- Minimize cost ($3 per serving of vegetables, $5 per serving of fruits):
  3 * Vegetables + 5 * Fruits
```python

# Decision Variables
Vegetables = intvar(0, 999999999)  # Number of servings of vegetables
Fruits = intvar(0, 999999999)  # Number of servings of fruits

Minerals = intvar(0, 999999999)

m += 3 * Vegetables <= Minerals

m += 1 * Fruits <= Minerals

# He wants to eat at least 20 units of vitamins and 30 units of minerals:
m += Vitamins >= 20
m += Minerals >= 30

# Objective

A teddy bear company produces three different colored bears: black, white, and brown. These bears are made in two different factories. Running factory 1 for 1 hour costs $300 and produces 5 black teddy bears, 6 white teddy bears, and 3 brown ones. Running factory 2 for 1 hour costs $600 and produces 10 black teddy bears and 10 white teddy bears. (but no brown ones). To meet children's demand, at least 20 black teddy bears, 5 white teddy bears, and 15 brown teddy bears must be made daily. Given this information, develop a linear programming problem assuming the teddy bear company wants to minimize the cost of production.
Decision Variables:
- Number of hours factory 1 runs: HoursFactory1
- Number of hours factory 2 runs: HoursFactory2

Constraints:
- To meet the daily demand of 20 black teddy bears:
  5 * HoursFactory1 + 10 * HoursFactory2 >= 20
- To meet the daily demand of 5 white teddy bears:
  6 * HoursFactory1 + 10 * HoursFactory2 >= 5
- To meet the daily demand of 15 brown teddy bears:
  3 * HoursFactory1 >= 15
- Non-negativity constraints:
  HoursFactory1 >= 0
  HoursFactory2 >= 0

Objective:
- Minimize the total cost of production:
  300 * HoursFactory1 + 600 * HoursFactory2
```python

from cpmpy import Model, intvar

# Decision Variables
HoursFactory1 = intvar(0, 999999999)  # Number of hours factory 1 runs
HoursFactory2 = intvar(0, 999999999)  # Number of hours factory 2 runs

# To meet the daily demand of 5 white teddy bears:
m += 6 * HoursFactory1 + 10 * HoursFactory2 >= 5
# To meet the daily demand of 15 brown teddy bears:
m += 3 * HoursFactory1 >= 15

# Non-negativity constraints:
m += HoursFactory1 >= 0
m += HoursFactory2 >= 0

# Objective
# Minimize the total cost of production:
m.minimize(300 * HoursFactory1 + 600 * HoursFactory2)

Since the high intensity drill produces a lot of noise pollution, at most 40% of the drills can be high intensity ones. Further, at least 10 should be low intensity drills. How many of each drill should be used to minimize the total number of drills needed?

- Number of low intensity drills used: LowIntensityDrills

  50 * HighIntensityDrills + 20 * LowIntensityDrills <= 700
- At most 40% of the drills can be high intensity:
  HighIntensityDrills <= 0.4 * (HighIntensityDrills + LowIntensityDrills)
- At least 10 drills should be low intensity:
  LowIntensityDrills >= 10

Objective:
- Minimize the total number of drills used:
  HighIntensityDrills + LowIntensityDrills

On the other hand, the hay harvester produces 3 kg of methane gas per acre and requires 1 kg of fuel. There are 300 kg of fuel available and the farmer can produce at most 800 kg of methane gas. For how many acres should each machine be used to maximize the amount of hay processed?
Decision Variables:
- Number of acres processed by the windrower: WindrowerAcres
- Number of acres processed by the hay harvester: HarvesterAcres

- Total acres processed should not exceed 200:
  WindrowerAcres + HarvesterAcres <= 200
- The windrower processes 10 kg of hay per acre:
  10 * WindrowerAcres <= TotalHayProcessed
- The hay harvester processes 8 kg of hay per acre:
  8 * HarvesterAcres <= TotalHayProcessed
- The windrower produces 5 kg of methane gas per acre:
  5 * WindrowerAcres <= 800
- The hay harvester produces 3 kg of methane gas per acre:
  3 * HarvesterAcres <= 800
- The windrower requires 2 kg of fuel per acre:
  2 * WindrowerAcres + 1 * HarvesterAcres <= 300

- Maximize the total amount of hay processed:
  TotalHayProcessed = 10 * WindrowerAcres + 8 * HarvesterAcres
```python

HarvesterAcres = intvar(0, 200)  # Number of acres processed by the hay harvester

m += WindrowerAcres + HarvesterAcres <= 200
# The windrower produces 10 kg of hay per acre:
m += 10 * WindrowerAcres <= 200
# The hay harvester produces 8 kg of hay per acre:
m += 8 * HarvesterAcres <= 200
# The windrower produces 5 kg of methane gas per acre:
m += 5 * WindrowerAcres <= 800
# The hay harvester produces 3 kg of methane gas per acre:
m += 3 * HarvesterAcres <= 800

A high rise building is buying two types of furnaces, a new model and an old model. A new model furnace can heat 10 apartments and consumes 200 kWh per day. An old model can heat 15 apartments and consumes 250 kWh per day. Since the old model is harder to find, at most 35% of the furnaces can be the old model and at least 5 new model furnaces should be used. If the high rise needs to heat at least 200 apartments and has 3500 kWh of electricity available, how many of each furnace should be purchase to minimize the total number of furnaces?
Decision Variables:
- Number of new model furnaces purchased: NewFurnaces
- Number of old model furnaces purchased: OldFurnaces

Constraints:
- Total number of apartments heated by new model furnaces:
  10 * NewFurnaces >= 200
- Total number of apartments heated by old model furnaces:
  15 * OldFurnaces >= 200
- Total number of apartments heated by all furnaces:
  10 * NewFurnaces + 15 * OldFurnaces >= 200
- Total electricity consumption by new model furnaces:
  200 * NewFurnaces <= 3500
- Total electricity consumption by old model furnaces:
  250 * OldFurnaces <= 3500
- At least 5 new model furnaces should be used:
  NewFurnaces >= 5
- At most 35% of the furnaces can be the old model:
  OldFurnaces <= 0.35 * (NewFurnaces + OldFurnaces)

Objective:
- Minimize the total number of furnaces purchased:
  NewFurnaces + OldFurnaces
```python

from cpmpy import Model, intvar

# Decision Variables
NewFurnaces = intvar(0, 999999999)  # Number of new model furnaces purchased
OldFurnaces = intvar(0, 999999999)  # Number of old model furnaces purchased

# Constraints
m = Model()

# Total number of apartments heated by new model furnaces:
m += 10 * NewFurnaces >= 200
# Total number of apartments heated by old model furnaces:
m += 15 * OldFurnaces >= 200
# Total number of apartments heated by all furnaces:
m += 10 * NewFurnaces + 15 * OldFurnaces >= 200
# Total electricity consumption by new model furnaces:
m += 200 * NewFurnaces <= 3500
# Total electricity consumption by old model furnaces:
m += 250 * OldFurnaces <= 3500
# At least 5 new model furnaces should be used:
m += NewFurnaces >= 5
# At most 35% of the furnaces can be the old model:
m += OldFurnaces <= 0.35 * (NewFurnaces + OldFurnaces)

# Objective
# Minimize the total number of furnaces purchased:
m.minimize(NewFurnaces + OldFurnaces)

An oil and gas company operates on 300 acres of land where they use oil wells of small and large size. Per acre of land, a small oil well can produce 2 barrels of oil. Per acre of land, a large oil well can produce 5 barrels of oil. However, a small oil well produces 10 units of pollution and requires 5 drill bits per acre and a large oil well produces 20 units of pollution and requires 10 drill bits per acre. The company has available 2500 drill bits and due to strict environmental laws can produce at most 4500 units of pollution. For how many acres should each oil well be used to maximize the total production of oil?
Decision Variables:
- Number of acres used for small oil wells: SmallOilWells
- Number of acres used for large oil wells: LargeOilWells

Constraints:
- Total acres used for oil wells should not exceed 300:
  SmallOilWells + LargeOilWells <= 300
- Small oil well produces 2 barrels of oil per acre:
  2 * SmallOilWells <= TotalOilSmall
- Large oil well produces 5 barrels of oil per acre:
  5 * LargeOilWells <= TotalOilLarge
- Small oil well produces 10 units of pollution and requires 5 drill bits per acre:
  10 * SmallOilWells + 5 * SmallOilWells <= 4500
- Large oil well produces 20 units of pollution and requires 10 drill bits per acre:
  20 * LargeOilWells + 10 * LargeOilWells <= 4500
- Total available drill bits:
  5 * SmallOilWells + 10 * LargeOilWells <= 2500

Objective:
- Maximize total production of oil:
  TotalOilSmall + TotalOilLarge
```python

from cpmpy import Model, intvar

# Decision Variables
SmallOilWells = intvar(0, 300)  # Number of acres used for small oil wells
LargeOilWells = intvar(0, 300)  # Number of acres used for large oil wells

# Total oil production variables
TotalOilSmall = 2 * SmallOilWells
TotalOilLarge = 5 * LargeOilWells

# Constraints
m = Model()

# Total acres used for oil wells should not exceed 300:
m += SmallOilWells + LargeOilWells <= 300
# Small oil well produces 2 barrels of oil per acre:
m += TotalOilSmall <= 300
# Large oil well produces 5 barrels of oil per acre:
m += TotalOilLarge <= 300
# Small oil well produces 10 units of pollution and requires 5 drill bits per acre:
m += 10 * SmallOilWells <= 4500
m += 5 * SmallOilWells <= 2500
# Large oil well produces 20 units of pollution and requires 10 drill bits per acre:
m += 20 * LargeOilWells <= 4500
m += 10 * LargeOilWells <= 2500

# Objective
# Maximize total production of oil:
m.maximize(TotalOilSmall + TotalOilLarge)

- Number of fiber supplemented brownies made: Brownies

- Each brownie requires 4 units of fiber and each lemon square requires 6 units of fiber:
  4 * Brownies + 6 * LemonSquares = TotalFiber
- Each brownie requires 5 units of chocolate mix and each lemon square requires 7 units of lemon mix:
  5 * Brownies <= 2500
  7 * LemonSquares <= 3300
- The number of lemon squares made must be larger than the number of brownies made:
  LemonSquares > Brownies

  TotalFiber

How many of each process should be used to maximize the amount of carbon dioxide produced?

- Number of processes with a catalyst: CatalystProcesses
- Number of processes without a catalyst: NoCatalystProcesses

Constraints:
- Wood constraint: 
  10 * CatalystProcesses + 15 * NoCatalystProcesses <= 300
- Oxygen constraint:
  20 * CatalystProcesses + 12 * NoCatalystProcesses <= 300
- Non-negativity constraint:
  CatalystProcesses >= 0
  NoCatalystProcesses >= 0

- Maximize the amount of carbon dioxide produced:
  15 * CatalystProcesses + 18 * NoCatalystProcesses

m += CatalystProcesses >= 0
m += NoCatalystProcesses >= 0

A factory has two machines, A and B. Each day, machine A can make 30 items and consumes 100 kWh. Machine B can make 50 items and consumes 120 kWh per day. The factory must produce at least 1000 items per day and has 3000 kWh of electricity available per day. Since there are not many workers that can operate both machines, at most 30% of the machines must be of type B. Further, at least 5 machines of type A should be used. How many of each machine should be used to minimize the total number of machines?
Decision Variables:
- Number of machines of type A used: MachinesA
- Number of machines of type B used: MachinesB

Constraints:
- Machine A can make 30 items per day:
  30 * MachinesA >= 1000
- Machine B can make 50 items per day:
  50 * MachinesB >= 1000
- Total items produced per day should be at least 1000:
  30 * MachinesA + 50 * MachinesB >= 1000
- Machine A consumes 100 kWh per day:
  100 * MachinesA <= 3000
- Machine B consumes 120 kWh per day:
  120 * MachinesB <= 3000
- Total electricity consumption should not exceed 3000 kWh per day:
  100 * MachinesA + 120 * MachinesB <= 3000
- At most 30% of the machines can be of type B:
  MachinesB <= 0.3 * (MachinesA + MachinesB)
- At least 5 machines of type A should be used:
  MachinesA >= 5

Objective:
- Minimize the total number of machines used:
  MachinesA + MachinesB
```python

from cpmpy import Model, intvar

# Decision Variables
MachinesA = intvar(0, 999999999)  # Number of machines of type A used
MachinesB = intvar(0, 999999999)  # Number of machines of type B used

m = Model()

# Machine A can make 30 items per day:
m += 30 * MachinesA >= 1000
# Machine B can make 50 items per day:
m += 50 * MachinesB >= 1000
# Total items produced per day should be at least 1000:
m += 30 * MachinesA + 50 * MachinesB >= 1000
# Machine A consumes 100 kWh per day:
m += 100 * MachinesA <= 3000
# Machine B consumes 120 kWh per day:
m += 120 * MachinesB <= 3000
# Total electricity consumption should not exceed 3000 kWh per day:
m += 100 * MachinesA + 120 * MachinesB <= 3000

m += MachinesB <= 0.3 * (MachinesA + MachinesB)
# At least 5 machines of type A should be used:
m += MachinesA >= 5

# Objective
# Minimize the total number of machines used:
m.minimize(MachinesA + MachinesB)

A chemical plant can buy two types of generators, generator A and generator B, which use two different processes to generate hydrogen. Generator A uses an electrolysis process and produces 40 cubic meters of hydrogen as well as 300 units of pollutants every day. Generator B uses a fermentation process to produce 30 cubic meters of hydrogen per day while outputting 200 units of pollutants. The chemical plant must make a minimum of 1000 cubic meters of hydrogen per day but due to environmental restrictions they can produce at most 3000 units of pollutant. How many of each type of generator should they buy to minimize the number of generators needed?
Decision Variables:
- Number of generator A units bought: GenA
- Number of generator B units bought: GenB

Constraints:
- Generator A produces 40 cubic meters of hydrogen and 300 units of pollutants per day:
  40 * GenA <= Hydrogen_A
  300 * GenA <= Pollutants_A
- Generator B produces 30 cubic meters of hydrogen and 200 units of pollutants per day:
  30 * GenB <= Hydrogen_B
  200 * GenB <= Pollutants_B
- The plant must produce at least 1000 cubic meters of hydrogen per day:
  Hydrogen_A + Hydrogen_B >= 1000
- The plant must produce at most 3000 units of pollutants per day:
  Pollutants_A + Pollutants_B <= 3000

Objective:
- Minimize the number of generators needed:
  GenA + GenB
```python

from cpmpy import Model, intvar

# Decision Variables
GenA = intvar(0, 999999999)  # Number of generator A units bought
GenB = intvar(0, 999999999)  # Number of generator B units bought

# Constants
Hydrogen_A = 40
Pollutants_A = 300
Hydrogen_B = 30
Pollutants_B = 200

# Constraints
m = Model()

# Generator A produces 40 cubic meters of hydrogen and 300 units of pollutants per day:
m += Hydrogen_A * GenA >= 40 * GenA
m += Pollutants_A * GenA >= 300 * GenA

# Generator B produces 30 cubic meters of hydrogen and 200 units of pollutants per day:
m += Hydrogen_B * GenB >= 30 * GenB
m += Pollutants_B * GenB >= 200 * GenB

# The plant must produce at least 1000 cubic meters of hydrogen per day:
m += Hydrogen_A * GenA + Hydrogen_B * GenB >= 1000

# The plant must produce at most 3000 units of pollutants per day:
m += Pollutants_A * GenA + Pollutants_B * GenB <= 3000

# Objective
# Minimize the number of generators needed:
m.minimize(GenA + GenB)

For each square mile of land, heap leaching technique can have a daily production of 3 tons of rare earth oxide per square miles but it also creates 8 tons of polluted wastewater and requires 10 extraction machines. On the other hand, vat leaching technique produces 5 tons of rare earth oxide per square miles per day while creating 17 tons of polluted wastewater and requiring 20 extraction machines. There are 100 machines available and due to environmental regulations, the amount of polluted wastewater must be at most 90 tons daily. Find the proportion of lands that use each mining technique in order to maximize the daily production of rare earth oxide.
Decision Variables:
- Number of square miles of land allocated to heap leaching: HeapLeaching
- Number of square miles of land allocated to vat leaching: VatLeaching

Constraints:
- Total available land is 100 square miles:
  HeapLeaching + VatLeaching <= 100
- Heap leaching requires 10 extraction machines per square mile and vat leaching requires 20 extraction machines per square mile:
  10 * HeapLeaching + 20 * VatLeaching <= 100
- Heap leaching produces 8 tons of polluted wastewater per square mile and vat leaching produces 17 tons of polluted wastewater per square mile:
  8 * HeapLeaching + 17 * VatLeaching <= 90

Objective:
- Maximize the daily production of rare earth oxide:
  3 * HeapLeaching + 5 * VatLeaching
```python

from cpmpy import Model, intvar

HeapLeaching = intvar(0, 100)  # Number of square miles of land allocated to heap leaching
VatLeaching = intvar(0, 100)  # Number of square miles of land allocated to vat leaching

# Constraints
m = Model()

# Total available land is 100 square miles:
m += HeapLeaching + VatLeaching <= 100
# Heap leaching requires 10 extraction machines per square mile and vat leaching requires 20 extraction machines per square mile:
m += 10 * HeapLeaching + 20 * VatLeaching <= 100
# Heap leaching produces 8 tons of polluted wastewater per square mile and vat leaching produces 17 tons of polluted wastewater per square mile:
m += 8 * HeapLeaching + 17 * VatLeaching <= 90

If each batch of vitamin shots can supply 10 people and each batch of vitamin pills can supply 7 people, how many batches of each should be made to maximize the number of people that can be supplied?

- Number of batches of vitamin shots made: Shots
- Number of batches of vitamin pills made: Pills

Constraints:
- Each batch of vitamin shots requires 30 units of vitamin C and 40 units of vitamin D:
  30 * Shots <= 1200 (Vitamin C constraint)
  40 * Shots <= 1500 (Vitamin D constraint)
- Each batch of vitamin pills requires 50 units of vitamin C and 30 units of vitamin D:
  50 * Pills <= 1200 (Vitamin C constraint)
  30 * Pills <= 1500 (Vitamin D constraint)
- The number of batches of vitamin pills must be larger than the number of batches of vitamin shots:
  Pills > Shots
- The clinic can make at most 10 batches of vitamin shots:
  Shots <= 10

Objective:
- Maximize the number of people that can be supplied (10 people per batch of shots, 7 people per batch of pills):
  10 * Shots + 7 * Pills

How many units of each should be added to the shampoo to minimize the total amount of time it takes for the mixture to be effective? (Note: one must be added before the other)
Decision Variables:
- Number of units of sulfate added to the shampoo: Sulfate
- Number of units of ginger added to the shampoo: Ginger

Constraints:
- The shampoo must contain at least 100 units of sulfate:
  Sulfate >= 100
- The total units of both ingredients should be 400:
  Sulfate + Ginger = 400
- There can be at most twice the amount of sulfate as ginger:
  Sulfate <= 2 * Ginger

Objective:
- Minimize the total time it takes for the mixture to be effective:
  0.5 * Sulfate + 0.75 * Ginger
```python

from cpmpy import Model, intvar

# Decision Variables
Sulfate = intvar(100, 400)  # Number of units of sulfate added to the shampoo
Ginger = intvar(0, 400)  # Number of units of ginger added to the shampoo

# Constraints
m = Model()

# The shampoo must contain at least 100 units of sulfate:
m += Sulfate >= 100
# The total units of both ingredients should be 400:
m += Sulfate + Ginger == 400
# There can be at most twice the amount of sulfate as ginger:
m += Sulfate <= 2 * Ginger

# Objective
# Minimize the total time it takes for the mixture to be effective:
m.minimize(0.5 * Sulfate + 0.75 * Ginger)

A pharmaceutical company has two labs, lab 1 and lab 2, where they make heart and lung medication in pill form. At lab 1, they can produce 20 heart medication pills and 30 lung medication pills per hour. At lab 2, they can produce 30 heart medication pills and 40 lung medication pills per hour. Each session at lab 1 requires 3 hours of worker labor while each session at lab 2 requires 5 hours of worker labor. The company has 1500 worker hours available and must make at least 20000 heart medication pills and at least 30000 lung medication pills. How many hours at each lab should be run to minimize the total time needed?
Decision Variables:
- Number of hours lab 1 is run: HoursLab1
- Number of hours lab 2 is run: HoursLab2

Constraints:
- Total worker hours available is 1500:
  3 * HoursLab1 + 5 * HoursLab2 <= 1500
- Must make at least 20000 heart medication pills:
  20 * HoursLab1 + 30 * HoursLab2 >= 20000
- Must make at least 30000 lung medication pills:
  30 * HoursLab1 + 40 * HoursLab2 >= 30000

Objective:
- Minimize the total time needed:
  HoursLab1 + HoursLab2
```python

HoursLab2 = intvar(0, 999999999)  # Number of hours lab 2 is run

# Total worker hours available is 1500:
m += 3 * HoursLab1 + 5 * HoursLab2 <= 1500
# Must make at least 20000 heart medication pills:
m += 20 * HoursLab1 + 30 * HoursLab2 >= 20000
# Must make at least 30000 lung medication pills:
m += 30 * HoursLab1 + 40 * HoursLab2 >= 30000

# Objective
# Minimize the total time needed:
m.minimize(HoursLab1 + HoursLab2)

The lab can make at most 5 doses of medicine A and the number of doses of medicine B must be larger than the number of dosed of medicine A. - Number of doses of medicine B: DosesB

- The lab has at most 400 units of mRNA:
  50 * DosesA + 30 * DosesB <= 400

  DosesA <= 5

  DosesB > DosesA

- Maximize the number of people that can be treated (12 people per dose of medicine A, 8 people per dose of medicine B):

- Number of swab tests administered: SwabTests

  10 * SpitTests + 15 * SwabTests <= 8000
- At least twice as many spit tests should be given as swabs:

  BeamBridges > TrussBridges

  40 * BeamBridges + 60 * TrussBridges

  6 * Vans + 3 * Cars >= 200
- At most 30% of the vehicles can be vans:
  Vans <= 0.3 * (Vans + Cars)

Objective:
- Minimize the total number of cars used:
  Cars
```python

Cars = intvar(0, 999999999)  # Number of cars used

m += 6 * Vans + 3 * Cars >= 200

m += Vans <= 0.3 * (Vans + Cars)

A toy store sells plush toys and dolls. Each plush toy costs the store $3 and each doll costs the store $2. The store owner can spend at most $700 on inventory. Each plush toy is then sold for a profit of $4 while each doll is sold for a profit of $2. The owner estimates that at least 90 plush toys but at most 190 plush toys are sold each month. He also estimates that the number of dolls sold is at most twice the amount of plush toys sold. How many of each should be bought and sold to maximize profit?

Decision Variables:
- Number of plush toys bought and sold: PlushToys
- Number of dolls bought and sold: Dolls

Constraints:
- The store owner can spend at most $700 on inventory:
  3 * PlushToys + 2 * Dolls <= 700
- At least 90 but at most 190 plush toys will be sold:
  90 <= PlushToys <= 190
- The number of dolls sold is at most twice the number of plush toys sold:
  Dolls <= 2 * PlushToys

Objective:
- Maximize profit ($4 profit per plush toy, $2 profit per doll):
  4 * PlushToys + 2 * Dolls
```python

from cpmpy import Model, intvar

# Decision Variables
PlushToys = intvar(0, 999999999)  # Number of plush toys bought and sold
Dolls = intvar(0, 999999999)  # Number of dolls bought and sold

# Constraints
m = Model()

# The store owner can spend at most $700 on inventory:
m += 3 * PlushToys + 2 * Dolls <= 700
# At least 90 but at most 190 plush toys will be sold:
m += PlushToys >= 90
m += PlushToys <= 190
# The number of dolls sold is at most twice the number of plush toys sold:
m += Dolls <= 2 * PlushToys

# Objective
# Maximize profit ($4 profit per plush toy, $2 profit per doll):
m.maximize(4 * PlushToys + 2 * Dolls)

Based on simple analysis, the woman determines her chance of losing her money would be 50% for basketball tournament, 25% for horse race, and 10% for the soccer game. The payout for each dollar put on each bet will be $1.2 for basketball tournament, $0.5 for horse race, and $0.1 for the soccer game. Knowing herself, she limits her average chance of losing her money should be at most 30%. Could you help her determine how much to money to put on each sport bet to maximize her average payout?
Decision Variables:
- Amount of money to put on the basketball tournament: BasketballMoney
- Amount of money to put on the horse race: HorseMoney
- Amount of money to put on the soccer game: SoccerMoney

Constraints:
- The total amount of money spent should not exceed $100000:
  BasketballMoney + HorseMoney + SoccerMoney <= 100000
- The average chance of losing money should be at most 30%:
  0.5 * BasketballMoney + 0.25 * HorseMoney + 0.1 * SoccerMoney <= 0.3 * (BasketballMoney + HorseMoney + SoccerMoney)

Objective:
- Maximize the average payout ($1.2 payout per dollar for basketball, $0.5 payout per dollar for horse race, $0.1 payout per dollar for soccer game):
  1.2 * BasketballMoney + 0.5 * HorseMoney + 0.1 * SoccerMoney
```python

from cpmpy import Model, intvar

# Decision Variables
BasketballMoney = intvar(0, 100000)  # Amount of money to put on the basketball tournament
HorseMoney = intvar(0, 100000)  # Amount of money to put on the horse race
SoccerMoney = intvar(0, 100000)  # Amount of money to put on the soccer game

# Constraints
m = Model()

# The total amount of money spent should not exceed $100000:
m += BasketballMoney + HorseMoney + SoccerMoney <= 100000
# The average chance of losing money should be at most 30%:
m += 0.5 * BasketballMoney + 0.25 * HorseMoney + 0.1 * SoccerMoney <= 0.3 * (BasketballMoney + HorseMoney + SoccerMoney)

# Objective
# Maximize the average payout ($1.2 payout per dollar for basketball, $0.5 payout per dollar for horse race, $0.1 payout per dollar for soccer game):
m.maximize(1.2 * BasketballMoney + 0.5 * HorseMoney + 0.1 * SoccerMoney)

```

A food company would like to run its commercials on three streaming platforms: Pi TV, Beta Video and Gamma Live. The cost for a commercial as well as the expected audience reach is given. On Pi TV, a commercial costs $1200 and attracts 2000 viewers. On Beta Video, a commercial costs $2000 and attracts 5000 viewers. On Gamma Live, a commercial costs $4000 and attracts 9000 viewers. Beta Video limits the number of commercials from a single company to 8. In order to attract a wide range of people, at most a third of all commercials should occur on Gamma Live and a minimum of 20% should occur on Pi TV. If the weekly budget is $20000, how many commercials should be run in each of the three possible choices in order to maximize audience?

Decision Variables:
- Number of commercials on Pi TV: CommercialsPiTV
- Number of commercials on Beta Video: CommercialsBetaVideo
- Number of commercials on Gamma Live: CommercialsGammaLive

Constraints:
- The total cost of commercials should not exceed the weekly budget of $20000:
  1200 * CommercialsPiTV + 2000 * CommercialsBetaVideo + 4000 * CommercialsGammaLive <= 20000
- Beta Video limits the number of commercials to 8:
  CommercialsBetaVideo <= 8
- At most a third of all commercials should occur on Gamma Live:
  CommercialsGammaLive <= (CommercialsPiTV + CommercialsBetaVideo + CommercialsGammaLive) / 3
- At least 20% of commercials should occur on Pi TV:
  CommercialsPiTV >= 0.2 * (CommercialsPiTV + CommercialsBetaVideo + CommercialsGammaLive)

Objective:
- Maximize the total audience reach:
  2000 * CommercialsPiTV + 5000 * CommercialsBetaVideo + 9000 * CommercialsGammaLive
```python

from cpmpy import Model, intvar

# Decision Variables
CommercialsPiTV = intvar(0, 999999999)  # Number of commercials on Pi TV
CommercialsBetaVideo = intvar(0, 8)  # Number of commercials on Beta Video (limited to 8)
CommercialsGammaLive = intvar(0, 999999999)  # Number of commercials on Gamma Live

# Constraints
m = Model()

# The total cost of commercials should not exceed the weekly budget of $20000:
m += 1200 * CommercialsPiTV + 2000 * CommercialsBetaVideo + 4000 * CommercialsGammaLive <= 20000
# At most a third of all commercials should occur on Gamma Live:
m += CommercialsGammaLive <= (CommercialsPiTV + CommercialsBetaVideo + CommercialsGammaLive) / 3
# At least 20% of commercials should occur on Pi TV:
m += CommercialsPiTV >= 0.2 * (CommercialsPiTV + CommercialsBetaVideo + CommercialsGammaLive)

# Objective
# Maximize the total audience reach:
m.maximize(2000 * CommercialsPiTV + 5000 * CommercialsBetaVideo + 9000 * CommercialsGammaLive)

Since the temperature check is recommended to be performed on most people, the testing station requires that the temperature check is performed at least 5 times as many as the blood test. If the disease testing station only has a total of 22000 staff minutes, how many of each test or check should be done to maximize the number of patients seen?
Decision Variables:
- Number of temperature checks performed: TemperatureChecks
- Number of blood tests conducted: BloodTests

- Each temperature check takes 2 minutes and each blood test takes 10 minutes, with a total of 22000 staff minutes available:
  2 * TemperatureChecks + 10 * BloodTests <= 22000
- At least 45 blood tests must be conducted:
  BloodTests >= 45
- The number of temperature checks performed should be at least 5 times the number of blood tests:
  TemperatureChecks >= 5 * BloodTests

- Maximize the number of patients seen (combination of temperature checks and blood tests):
  TemperatureChecks + BloodTests

# At least 45 blood tests must be conducted:
m += BloodTests >= 45

A concert organizer has to transport equipment using carts or trolleys. Carts can transport 5 kg/min of equipment and requires 2 workers. Trolleys can transport 7 kg/min of equipment and requires 4 workers. There must be at least 12 trolleys to be used. Additionally, only a maximum of 40% of the transportation can be using trolleys. The organizer has to deliver at a rate of 100 kg/min of equipment. How many of each transportation method should be used to minimize the total number of workers?
Decision Variables:
- Number of carts used: Carts
- Number of trolleys used: Trolleys

Constraints:
- Each cart can transport 5 kg/min and each trolley can transport 7 kg/min:
  5 * Carts + 7 * Trolleys >= 100
- Each cart requires 2 workers and each trolley requires 4 workers:
  2 * Carts + 4 * Trolleys = TotalWorkers
- At least 12 trolleys must be used:
  Trolleys >= 12
- Maximum 40% of transportation can be using trolleys:
  Trolleys <= 0.4 * (Carts + Trolleys)

Objective:
- Minimize the total number of workers:
  TotalWorkers
```python

from cpmpy import Model, intvar

# Decision Variables
Carts = intvar(0, 999999999)  # Number of carts used
Trolleys = intvar(0, 999999999)  # Number of trolleys used
TotalWorkers = intvar(0, 999999999)  # Total number of workers

# Constraints
m = Model()

# Each cart can transport 5 kg/min and each trolley can transport 7 kg/min:
m += 5 * Carts + 7 * Trolleys >= 100
# Each cart requires 2 workers and each trolley requires 4 workers:
m += 2 * Carts + 4 * Trolleys == TotalWorkers
# At least 12 trolleys must be used:
m += Trolleys >= 12
# Maximum 40% of transportation can be using trolleys:
m += Trolleys <= 0.4 * (Carts + Trolleys)

# Objective
# Minimize the total number of workers:
m.minimize(TotalWorkers)

An extremely large ski resort is looking into purchasing two types of ski lifts, a densely-seated one and a loosely-seated one. The densely-seated ski lift is able to bring 45 guests up the slopes every minute whereas the loosely-seated ski lift can transport 20 guests every minute.  The densely-seated ski lift uses 30 units of electricity and the loosely-seated lift uses 22 units of electricity. There must be at least five loosely-seated ski lifts because they move slower and are friendlier for beginners. The ski resort needs at least 1000 guests every minute to make a profit and has available 940 units of electricity. How many of each type of ski lifts should they plan to install to minimize the total number of ski lifts needed?
Decision Variables:
- Number of densely-seated ski lifts: DenselySeatedLifts
- Number of loosely-seated ski lifts: LooselySeatedLifts

Constraints:
- The total number of guests transported per minute should be at least 1000:
  45 * DenselySeatedLifts + 20 * LooselySeatedLifts >= 1000
- The total electricity units used should not exceed 940:
  30 * DenselySeatedLifts + 22 * LooselySeatedLifts <= 940
- There must be at least 5 loosely-seated ski lifts:
  LooselySeatedLifts >= 5

Objective:
- Minimize the total number of ski lifts needed:
  DenselySeatedLifts + LooselySeatedLifts
```python

from cpmpy import Model, intvar

# Decision Variables
DenselySeatedLifts = intvar(0, 999999999)  # Number of densely-seated ski lifts
LooselySeatedLifts = intvar(0, 999999999)  # Number of loosely-seated ski lifts

# Constraints
m = Model()

# The total number of guests transported per minute should be at least 1000:
m += 45 * DenselySeatedLifts + 20 * LooselySeatedLifts >= 1000
# The total electricity units used should not exceed 940:
m += 30 * DenselySeatedLifts + 22 * LooselySeatedLifts <= 940
# There must be at least 5 loosely-seated ski lifts:
m += LooselySeatedLifts >= 5

Every day, the oil and gas company needs to meet the demands of at least 150000 US gallons of gas and they have 160 technicians that are on their staff. Since the high-volume pipe has a higher risk of environmental damage, at most 35 percent of the pipes can be high-volume ones. Additionally, there must be a minimum of 8 low-volume pipes.   Minimize SodiumIntake

- Number of mechanical keyboards manufactured: MechanicalKeyboards
- Number of standard keyboards manufactured: StandardKeyboards

Constraints:
- The manufacturer aims to have five times as many mechanical keyboards as standard keyboards:
  MechanicalKeyboards == 5 * StandardKeyboards
- A mechanical keyboard costs 5 units of plastic and 2 units of solder:
  5 * MechanicalKeyboards + 2 * StandardKeyboards <= 1000 (plastic constraint)
  2 * MechanicalKeyboards + 1 * StandardKeyboards <= 250 (solder constraint)

  MechanicalKeyboards + StandardKeyboards

  TotalProbes
